<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Proto-Germanic language</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">  (Redirected from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic&amp;redirect=no" title="Proto-Germanic">Proto-Germanic</a>)</span></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;width: 22em;">
<tr>
<td style="width:1px"></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;"><b>This article contains characters used to write reconstructed <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a> words.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:Special_characters" title="Help:Special characters">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> combining characters and <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin</a> characters.</td>

</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:247px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pre-roman_iron_age_(map).PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="657" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Pre-roman_iron_age_%28map%29.PNG/245px-Pre-roman_iron_age_%28map%29.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Pre-roman_iron_age_%28map%29.PNG/368px-Pre-roman_iron_age_%28map%29.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Pre-roman_iron_age_%28map%29.PNG/490px-Pre-roman_iron_age_%28map%29.PNG 2x" width="245"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pre-roman_iron_age_(map).PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_Iron_Age_in_Northern_Europe" title="Pre-Roman Iron Age in Northern Europe">pre-Roman Iron Age in Northern Europe</a> showing cultures associated with Proto-Germanic, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 500 BC. The red shows the area of the preceding <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Bronze_Age" title="Nordic Bronze Age">Nordic Bronze Age</a> in <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>; the magenta-colored area towards the south represents the <a href="/wiki/Jastorf_culture" title="Jastorf culture">Jastorf culture</a> of the <a href="/wiki/North_German_Plain" title="North German Plain">North German Plain</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Proto-Germanic</b> (abbreviated <b>PGmc</b>; German <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Urgermanisch</span></i>; also called <b>Common Germanic</b>, German <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Gemeingermanisch</span></i>) is the <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_reconstruction" title="Linguistic reconstruction">reconstructed</a> <a href="/wiki/Proto-language" title="Proto-language">proto-language</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic branch</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a>.</p>
<p>Proto-Germanic developed from pre-Proto-Germanic into three branches during the first half of the first millennium of the <a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">Common Era</a>: <a href="/wiki/West_Germanic_languages" title="West Germanic languages">West Germanic</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Germanic_languages" title="East Germanic languages">East Germanic</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Germanic_languages" title="North Germanic languages">North Germanic</a>, which however remained in <a href="/wiki/Language_contact" title="Language contact">contact</a> over a considerable time, especially the <a href="/wiki/Ingvaeonic_languages" title="Ingvaeonic languages">Ingvaeonic languages</a> (including <a href="/wiki/History_of_English" title="History of English">English</a>), which arose from West Germanic dialects which remained in continued contact with North Germanic.</p>
<p>A defining feature of Proto-Germanic is the completion of <a href="/wiki/Grimm%27s_law" title="Grimm's law">Grimm's law</a>, a set of sound changes that occurred between its status as a dialect of <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a> and its gradual divergence into a separate language. As it is probable that the development of this sound shift spanned a considerable time (several centuries), Proto-Germanic cannot adequately be reconstructed as a simple node in a <a href="/wiki/Tree_model" title="Tree model">tree model</a> but rather represents a phase of development that may span close to a thousand years. The end of the Common Germanic period is reached with the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Migration_Period" title="Migration Period">Migration Period</a> in the fourth century.</p>
<p>The alternative term "<a href="/wiki/Germanic_parent_language" title="Germanic parent language">Germanic parent language</a>" may be used to include a larger scope of linguistic developments, spanning the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Bronze_Age" title="Nordic Bronze Age">Nordic Bronze Age</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_Iron_Age_in_Northern_Europe" title="Pre-Roman Iron Age in Northern Europe">Pre-Roman Iron Age in Northern Europe</a> (second to first millennia BC) to include "Pre-Germanic" (PreGmc), "Early Proto Germanic" (EPGmc) and "Late Proto-Germanic" (LPGmc).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> While Proto-Germanic refers only to the most recent reconstruction of the common ancestor of Germanic languages, the Germanic parent language refers to the entire journey that the dialect of Proto-Indo-European that would become Proto-Germanic underwent through the millennia.</p>
<p>The Proto-Germanic language is not directly attested by any coherent surviving texts; it has been <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_reconstruction" title="Linguistic reconstruction">reconstructed</a> using the <a href="/wiki/Comparative_method_(linguistics)" title="Comparative method (linguistics)">comparative method</a>. Fragmentary direct attestation exists of (late) Common Germanic in early <a href="/wiki/Runic_inscriptions" title="Runic inscriptions">runic inscriptions</a> (specifically the second-century AD <a href="/wiki/Vimose_inscriptions" title="Vimose inscriptions">Vimose inscriptions</a> and the second-century BC <a href="/wiki/Negau_helmet" title="Negau helmet">Negau helmet</a> inscription),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Comrie_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Comrie-2">[2]</a></sup> and in <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> era transcriptions of individual words (notably in <a href="/wiki/Tacitus" title="Tacitus">Tacitus</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Germania_(book)" title="Germania (book)">Germania</a></i>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 90 CE<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup>).</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Archaeology_and_early_historiography">Archaeology and early historiography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Archaeology and early historiography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:247px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Germanic_tribes_(750BC-1AD).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="376" data-file-width="537" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Germanic_tribes_%28750BC-1AD%29.png/245px-Germanic_tribes_%28750BC-1AD%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Germanic_tribes_%28750BC-1AD%29.png/368px-Germanic_tribes_%28750BC-1AD%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Germanic_tribes_%28750BC-1AD%29.png/490px-Germanic_tribes_%28750BC-1AD%29.png 2x" width="245"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Germanic_tribes_(750BC-1AD).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The expansion of the Germanic tribes<br/>
750 BC – AD 1 (after <a href="/wiki/The_Penguin_Atlas_of_World_History" title="The Penguin Atlas of World History">The Penguin Atlas of World History</a>, 1988):
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #f00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span>  Settlements before 750 BC</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #f84; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span>  New settlements 750–500 BC</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span>  New settlements 500–250 BC</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0f0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span>  New settlements 250 BC – AD 1</div>
Some sources also give a date of 750 BC for the earliest expansion out of southern Scandinavia along the North Sea coast towards the mouth of the Rhine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">[4]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oksywie_Wielbark_Przeworsk.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="626" data-file-width="830" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Oksywie_Wielbark_Przeworsk.gif/220px-Oksywie_Wielbark_Przeworsk.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Oksywie_Wielbark_Przeworsk.gif/330px-Oksywie_Wielbark_Przeworsk.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Oksywie_Wielbark_Przeworsk.gif/440px-Oksywie_Wielbark_Przeworsk.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oksywie_Wielbark_Przeworsk.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Germanic" title="East Germanic">East Germanic</a> expansion (1st and 2nd centuries AD): <a href="/wiki/Jastorf_culture" title="Jastorf culture">Jastorf culture</a> (blue), <a href="/wiki/Oksywie_culture" title="Oksywie culture">Oksywie culture</a> (red), <a href="/wiki/Przeworsk_culture" title="Przeworsk culture">Przeworsk culture</a> (yellow/orange); eastward expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Wielbark_culture" title="Wielbark culture">Wielbark culture</a> (light-red/orange).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Proto-Germanic language developed in southern Scandinavia (Denmark, south Sweden and southern Norway), the <i>Urheimat</i> (original home) of the Germanic tribes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> It is possible that Indo-European speakers first arrived in southern Scandinavia with the <a href="/wiki/Corded_Ware_culture" title="Corded Ware culture">Corded Ware culture</a> in the mid-3rd millennium BC, developing into the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Bronze_Age" title="Nordic Bronze Age">Nordic Bronze Age</a> cultures by the early 2nd millennium BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Proto-Germanic developed out of <a href="/wiki/Germanic_parent_language" title="Germanic parent language">pre-Proto-Germanic</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_Iron_Age" title="Pre-Roman Iron Age">Pre-Roman Iron Age</a> of Northern Europe. According to the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_substrate_hypothesis" title="Germanic substrate hypothesis">Germanic substrate hypothesis</a>, it may be influenced by non-Indo-European cultures, such as the <a href="/wiki/Funnelbeaker_culture" title="Funnelbeaker culture">Funnelbeaker culture</a>, but the sound change in the Germanic languages known as <a href="/wiki/Grimm%27s_law" title="Grimm's law">Grimm's law</a> points to a non-substratic development away from other branches of Indo-European.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[note 1]</a></sup> Proto-Germanic itself was likely spoken after <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 500 BC,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-Norse" title="Proto-Norse">Proto-Norse</a> from the 2nd century AD and later is still quite close to reconstructed Proto-Germanic, but other common innovations separating Germanic from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European" title="Proto-Indo-European">Proto-Indo-European</a> suggest a common history of pre-Proto-Germanic speakers throughout the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Bronze_Age" title="Nordic Bronze Age">Nordic Bronze Age</a>.</p>
<p>Early Germanic expansion in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_Iron_Age" title="Pre-Roman Iron Age">Pre-Roman Iron Age</a> (5th to 1st centuries BC) placed Proto-Germanic speakers in contact with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continental_Celtic" title="Continental Celtic">Continental Celtic</a> <a href="/wiki/La_T%C3%A8ne_culture" title="La Tène culture">La Tène horizon</a>.</p>
<p>A number of Celtic loanwords in Proto-Germanic have been identified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> By the 1st century AD, Germanic expansion reaches the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Rhine" title="Upper Rhine">Upper Rhine</a> in the south, and the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic peoples</a> first enter the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_historians" title="Roman historians">historical record</a>. At about the same time, extending east of the <a href="/wiki/Vistula" title="Vistula">Vistula</a> (<a href="/wiki/Oksywie_culture" title="Oksywie culture">Oksywie culture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Przeworsk_culture" title="Przeworsk culture">Przeworsk culture</a>), Germanic speakers come into contact with early <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavic</a> cultures, as reflected in early Germanic <a href="/wiki/Proto-Slavic_borrowings#Slavic_and_Germanic" title="Proto-Slavic borrowings">loans in Proto-Slavic</a>.</p>
<p>By the 3rd century, LPGmc speakers had expanded over significant distance, from the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dniepr" title="Dniepr">Dniepr</a> spanning about 1,200 km (700 mi). The period marks the breakup of Late Proto-Germanic and the beginning of the (historiographically-recorded) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germanic_migrations" title="Germanic migrations">Germanic migrations</a>. The first coherent text recorded in a Germanic language is the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Bible" title="Gothic Bible">Gothic Bible</a>, written in the later 4th century in the language of the <a href="/wiki/Thervingi" title="Thervingi">Thervingi</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gothic_Christians" title="Gothic Christians">Gothic Christians</a>, who had escaped <a href="/wiki/Gothic_persecution_of_Christians" title="Gothic persecution of Christians">persecution</a> by moving from Scythia to <a href="/wiki/Moesia" title="Moesia">Moesia</a> in 348.</p>
<p>The earliest coherent text (complete sentences including verbs) in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-Norse" title="Proto-Norse">Proto-Norse</a> become available c. 400 in <a href="/wiki/Runic_inscriptions" title="Runic inscriptions">runic inscriptions</a> (such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tune_Runestone" title="Tune Runestone">Tune Runestone</a>). The delineation of Late Common Germanic from Proto-Norse about then is largely a matter of convention. Early West Germanic becomes available in the 5th century with the <a href="/wiki/Frankish_language" title="Frankish language">Frankish</a> <a href="/wiki/Bergakker_inscription" title="Bergakker inscription">Bergakker inscription</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution">Evolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Evolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The evolution of Proto-Germanic from its ancestral forms, beginning with its ancestor <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a>, began with the development of a separate common way of speech among some geographically nearby speakers of a prior language and ended with the dispersion of the proto-language speakers into distinct populations with mostly independent speech habits. Between the two points, many sound changes occurred.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theories_of_phylogeny">Theories of phylogeny</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Theories of phylogeny">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Solutions">Solutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Solutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Phylogenetic_tree" title="Phylogenetic tree">Phylogeny</a> as applied to <a href="/wiki/Historical_linguistics" title="Historical linguistics">historical linguistics</a> involves the evolutionary descent of languages. The phylogeny problem is the question of what specific tree, in the <a href="/wiki/Tree_model" title="Tree model">tree model</a> of language evolution, best explains the paths of descent of all the members of a language family from a common language, or proto-language (at the root of the tree) to the attested languages (at the leaves of the tree). The <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic languages</a> form a tree with Proto-Germanic at its root that is a branch of the Indo-European tree, which in turn has <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a> at its root. Borrowing of lexical items from contact languages makes the relative position of the Germanic branch within Indo-European less clear than the positions of the other branches of Indo-European. In the course of the development of historical linguistics, various solutions have been proposed, none certain and all debatable.</p>
<p>In the evolutionary history of a language family, philologists consider a genetic "tree model" appropriate only if communities do not remain in effective contact as their languages diverge. Early Indo-European had limited contact between distinct lineages, and, uniquely, the Germanic subfamily exhibited a less treelike behaviour, as some of its characteristics were acquired from neighbours early in its evolution rather than from its direct ancestors. The internal diversification of West Germanic developed in an especially non-treelike manner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Proto-Germanic is generally agreed to have begun about 500 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> Its hypothetical ancestor between the end of Proto-Indo-European and 500 BC is termed <a href="/wiki/Germanic_parent_language" title="Germanic parent language">Pre-Proto-Germanic</a>. Whether it is to be included under a wider meaning of Proto-Germanic is a matter of usage.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Winfred_P._Lehmann" title="Winfred P. Lehmann">Winfred P. Lehmann</a> regarded <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Grimm" title="Jacob Grimm">Jacob Grimm</a>'s "First Germanic Sound Shift", or Grimm's law, and <a href="/wiki/Verner%27s_law" title="Verner's law">Verner's law</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> (which pertained mainly to consonants and were considered for many decades to have generated Proto-Germanic) as pre-Proto-Germanic and held that the "upper boundary" was the fixing of the accent, or stress, on the root syllable of a word, typically on the first syllable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> Proto-Indo-European had featured a moveable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitch-accent" title="Pitch-accent">pitch-accent</a> comprising "an alternation of high and low tones"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> as well as stress of position determined by a set of rules based on the lengths of a word's syllables.</p>
<p>The fixation of the stress led to sound changes in unstressed syllables. For Lehmann, the "lower boundary" was the dropping of final -a or -e in unstressed syllables; for example, post-PIE <i>*wóyd-e</i> &gt; Gothic <i>wait</i>, "knows". Antonsen agreed with Lehmann about the upper boundary<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> but later found <a href="/wiki/Runes" title="Runes">runic evidence</a> that the -a was not dropped: <i>ékwakraz … wraita</i>, "I, Wakraz, … wrote (this)". He says: "We must therefore search for a new lower boundary for Proto-Germanic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Antonsen's own scheme divides Proto-Germanic into an early stage and a late stage. The early stage includes the stress fixation and resulting "spontaneous vowel-shifts" while the late stage is defined by ten complex rules governing changes of both vowels and consonants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 250 BC Proto-Germanic had branched into five groups of Germanic: two each in the West and the North and one in the East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonological_stages_from_Proto-Indo-European_to_end_of_Proto-Germanic">Phonological stages from Proto-Indo-European to end of Proto-Germanic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Phonological stages from Proto-Indo-European to end of Proto-Germanic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germanic_Parent_Language" title="Germanic Parent Language">Germanic Parent Language</a></div>
<p>The following changes are known or presumed to have occurred in the history of Proto-Germanic in the wider sense from the end of Proto-Indo-European up to the point that Proto-Germanic began to break into mutually unintelligible dialects. The changes are listed roughly in chronological order, with changes that operate on the outcome of earlier ones appearing later in the list. The stages distinguished and the changes associated with each stage rely heavily on <a href="#CITEREFRinge2006">Ringe 2006</a>, Chapter 3, "The development of Proto-Germanic". Ringe in turn summarizes standard concepts and terminology.</p>
<h4><span id="Pre-Proto-Germanic_(Pre-PGmc)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Proto-Germanic_.28Pre-PGmc.29">Pre-Proto-Germanic (Pre-PGmc)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Pre-Proto-Germanic (Pre-PGmc)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>This stage began with the separation of a distinct speech, perhaps while it was still forming part of the Proto-Indo-European dialect continuum. It contained many innovations that were shared with other Indo-European branches to various degrees, probably through areal contacts, and mutual intelligibility with other dialects would have remained for some time. It was nevertheless on its own path, whether dialect or language.</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<td>Merging of PIE "palatovelar" and "velar" plosives ("centumization"):
<ul>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ḱ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/k/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ḱm̥tóm</span> "hundred" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*km̥tóm</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hundą</span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ǵ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/g/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wérǵom</span> "work" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wérgom</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*werką</span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ǵʰ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/gʰ/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ǵʰóstis</span> "stranger" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gʰóstis</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gastiz</span> "guest"</li>
<li>The actual pronunciation of the "palatovelar" and "velar" series is not reconstructible; it may be that the "palatovelars" were actually plain velars, and the "velars" were pronounced even farther back (post-velar or uvular) so it may be more accurate to say that, for example, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/k/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ḱ/</span> (see e.g. Ringe 2006, p. 87). Some also claim that the two series may not even have been distinct in PIE. See <a href="/wiki/Centum_and_satem_languages" title="Centum and satem languages">centum and satem languages</a>.</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Epenthesis" title="Epenthesis">Epenthesis</a> of <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/u/</span></b> before the syllabic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sonorants" title="Sonorants">sonorants</a>:
<ul>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/m̥/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/um/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ḱm̥tóm</span> "hundred" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kumtóm</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hundą</span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/n̥/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/un/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*n̥tér</span> "inside" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*untér</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*under</span> "among"</li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/l̥/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ul/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wĺ̥kʷos</span> "wolf" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wúlkʷos</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wulfaz</span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/r̥/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ur/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wŕ̥mis</span> "worm" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wurmis</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wurmiz</span></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>

<td><b>An epenthetic <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/s/</span></b> was inserted already in PIE after dental consonants when they were followed by a suffix beginning with a dental.
<ul>
<li>This sequence now becomes <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/TsT/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ts/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ss/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wid-tós</span> "known" (pronounced <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*widstos</span>) &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*witstós</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wissós</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wissaz</span> "certain"</span></li>
<li>A single example exists where <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/tt/</span> was word-internal, in which case it remained (even after <a href="/wiki/Grimm%27s_law" title="Grimm's law">Grimm's law</a> below)— <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*atta</span> "dad" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*attô</span></span></li>
</ul>

</tr>
<tr>
<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geminate" title="Geminate">Geminate</a> consonants are shortened</b> after a consonant or a long vowel — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*káyd-tis</span> "act of calling" (pronounced <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*káydstis</span>) &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*káyssis</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*káysis</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*haisiz</span> "command"</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Word-final long vowels are lengthened</b> to "overlong" vowels — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*séh₁mō</span> "seeds" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*séh₁mô</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sēmô</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Loss of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glottal_consonants" title="Glottal consonants">laryngeals</a></b>, phonemicising the <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">allophones</a> of <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/e/</span>:
<ul>
<li>Word-initial laryngeals are lost before a consonant — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₁dóntm̥</span> "tooth, acc." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dóntum</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tanþų</span></span></li>
<li>Laryngeals are lost before vowels:
<ul>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/h₁V/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/V/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₁ésti</span> "is" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ésti</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*isti</span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/h₂e/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/a/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/h₂V/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/V/</span> otherwise — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₂énti</span> "in front" &gt; (with shift of accent) <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*antí</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*andi</span> "in addition"</span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/h₃e/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/o/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/h₃V/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/V/</span> otherwise — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₃érō</span> "eagle" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*órô</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*arô</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Laryngeals are lost after vowels but lengthen the preceding vowel: <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/VH/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/Vː/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*séh₁mō</span> "seeds" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sēmô</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sēmô</span></span>
<ul>
<li>Two vowels that come to stand in <a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(linguistics)" title="Hiatus (linguistics)">hiatus</a> because of that change contract into an overlong vowel — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-oHom</span> "genitive plural" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ôm</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ǫ̂</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-eh₂es</span> "eh₂-stem nom. pl." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-âs</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ôz</span></span></li>
<li>In word-final position, the resulting long vowels remain distinct from (shorter than) the overlong vowels that were formed from PIE word-final long vowels — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-oh₂</span> "thematic 1st sg." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ō</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Laryngeals remain between consonants.</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Cowgill%27s_law" title="Cowgill's law">Cowgill's law</a></b>: <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/h₃/</span> (and possibly <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/h₂/</span>) is strengthened to <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/g/</span> between a sonorant and <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/w/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*n̥h₃mé</span> "us two" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*n̥h₃wé</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ungwé</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*unk</span></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Vocalisation of remaining laryngeals</b>: <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/H/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ə/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ph₂tḗr</span> "father" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*pətḗr</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*fadēr</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sámh₂dʰos</span> "sand" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sámədʰos</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*samdaz</span></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Velars are labialised</b> by following <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/w/</span>: <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*éḱwos</span> "horse" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ékwos</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ékʷos</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ehwaz</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Labiovelars are delabialised</b> next to <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/u/</span> (or <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/un/</span>) and before <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/t/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gʷʰénti-</span> ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gʷʰn̥tí-</span> "killing" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gʷʰúntis</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gʰúntis</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gunþiz</span> "battle"</span>
<ul>
<li>This rule continued to operate into the Proto-Germanic period.</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Proto-Germanic">Early Proto-Germanic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Early Proto-Germanic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>This stage began its evolution as a dialect of <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a> that had lost its laryngeals and had five long and six short vowels as well as one or two overlong vowels. The consonant system was still that of PIE minus palatovelars and laryngeals, but the loss of syllabic resonants already made the language markedly different from PIE proper. Mutual intelligibility might have still existed with other descendants of PIE, but it would have been strained, and the period marked the definitive break of Germanic from the other Indo-European languages and the beginning of Germanic proper, containing most of the sound changes that are now held to define this branch distinctively. This stage contained various consonant and vowel shifts, the loss of the contrastive accent inherited from PIE for a uniform accent on the first syllable of the word root, and the beginnings of the reduction of the resulting unstressed syllables.</p>
<p><span id="Loss_of_word-final_non-high_short_vowels"></span></p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<td><b>Loss of word-final non-high short vowels</b> <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/e/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/a/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/o/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wóyde</span> "(s)he knows" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wóyd</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wait</span>
<ul>
<li>A <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/j/</span> or <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/w/</span> preceding the vowel is also lost — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tósyo</span> "of that" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tós</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þas</span></li>
<li>Single-syllable words were not affected, but clitics were — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-kʷe</span> "and" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-kʷ</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-hw</span></li>
<li>When the lost vowel was accented, the accent shifted to the preceding syllable — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*n̥smé</span> "us" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*n̥swé</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*unswé</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*úns</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*uns</span></span> (not <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*unz</span>, showing that loss occurred before Verner's law)</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Grimm%27s_law" title="Grimm's law">Grimm's law</a></b>: Chain shift of the three series of plosives. Voiced plosives had already been devoiced before a voiceless obstruent prior to this stage. Labiovelars were delabialised before <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/t/</span>.
<ul>
<li>Voiceless plosives become fricatives, unless preceded by another obstruent. In a sequence of two voiceless obstruents, the second obstruent remains a plosive.
<ul>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/p/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɸ/</span> (<span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">f</span>) — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ph₂tḗr</span> "father" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*fəþḗr</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*fadēr</span></span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/t/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/θ/</span> (<span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">þ</span>) — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tód</span> "that" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þód</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þat</span></span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/k/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/x/</span> (<span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">h</span>) — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kátus</span> "fight" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*háþus</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*haþuz</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₂eǵs-</span> "axle" &gt; (devoicing) <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*aks-</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ahs-</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ahsō</span></span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/kʷ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/xʷ/</span> (<span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">hw</span>) — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kʷód</span> "what" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hʷód</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hwat</span></span></li>
<li>Since the second of two obstruents is unaffected, the sequences <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/sp/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/st/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/sk/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/skʷ/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/tt/</span> (only in <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*atta</span> "dad") remain.</li>
<li>The above also forms the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_spirant_law" title="Germanic spirant law">Germanic spirant law</a>:
<ul>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/bt/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/bʰt/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/pt/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɸt/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kh₂ptós</span> "grabbed" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kəptós</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*həftós</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*haftaz</span> "captive"</span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/gt/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/gʰt/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/kt/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/xt/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*oḱtṓw</span> "eight" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*oktṓw</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ohtṓw</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ahtōu</span></span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/gʷt/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/gʷʰt/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/kʷt/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/xt/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*nokʷtm̥</span> "night, acc." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*noktum</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*nohtum</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*nahtų</span></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Voiced plosives are devoiced:
<ul>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/b/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/p/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dʰewbu-</span> "deep" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dʰewpu-</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dewpu-</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*deupaz</span></span> (reformed as a-stem)</li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/d/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/t/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₁dóntm̥</span> "tooth, acc." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tónþum</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tanþų</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kʷód</span> "what" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hʷód</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hwat</span></span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/g/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/k/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wérǵom</span> "work" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wérgom</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*wérkom</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*werką</span></span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/gʷ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/kʷ/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gʷémeti</span> "(s)he will step, subj." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kʷémeþi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kwimidi</span> "(s)he comes"</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Aspirated plosives become voiced plosives or fricatives (see below):
<ul>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/bʰ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/b/</span> (<span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">[b,β]</span>) — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*bʰéreti</span> "(s)he is carrying" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*béreþi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*biridi</span></span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/dʰ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/d/</span> (<span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">[d,ð]</span>) — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dʰóh₁mos</span> "thing put" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dṓmos</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dōmaz</span> "judgement"</span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/gʰ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/g/</span> (<span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">[g,ɣ]</span>) — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gʰáns</span> "goose" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gáns</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gans</span></span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/gʷʰ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/gʷ/</span> (<span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">[gʷ,ɣʷ]</span>) — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sóngʷʰos</span> "chant" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sóngʷos</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sangwaz</span> "song"</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Verner%27s_law" title="Verner's law">Verner's law</a></b>: voiceless fricatives are voiced, allophonically at first, when they are preceded by an unaccented syllable:
<ul>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɸ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">[β]</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*upéri</span> "over" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*uféri</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ubéri</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ubiri</span></span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/θ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">[ð]</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tewtéh₂</span> "tribe" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þewþā́</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þewdā́</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þeudō</span></span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/x/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">[ɣ]</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₂yuHn̥ḱós</span> "young" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*yunkós</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*yunhós</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*yungós</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*jungaz</span></span> (with -z by analogy)</li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/xʷ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">[ɣʷ]</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kʷekʷléh₂</span> "wheels (collective)" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hʷehʷlā́</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hʷegʷlā́</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hweulō</span></span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/s/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">[z]</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₁régʷeses</span> "of darkness" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*rékʷeses</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*rékʷezez</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*rikwiziz</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kʷékʷlos</span> "wheel" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hʷéhʷlos</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hʷéhʷloz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hwehwlaz</span></li>
<li>Some small words that were generally unaccented were also affected — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₁ésmi</span>, unstressed <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₁esmi</span> "I am" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*esmi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ezmi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*immi</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₁sénti</span>, unstressed <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₁senti</span> "they are" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*senþi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sendi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sindi</span> (the stressed variants, which would have become <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ismi</span> and <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sinþi</span>, were lost)</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>All words become stressed on their first syllable</b>. The PIE contrastive accent is lost, phonemicising the voicing distinction created by Verner's law.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Word-initial <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/gʷ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/b/</span></b> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gʷʰédʰyeti</span> "(s)he is asking for" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gʷédyedi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*bédyedi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*bidiþi</span> "(s)he asks, (s)he prays"</span> (with -þ- by analogy)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Assimilation of sonorants</b>:
<ul>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/nw/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/nn/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ténh₂us</span> "thin" ~ fem. <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tn̥h₂éwih₂</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tn̥h₂ús</span> ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tn̥h₂wíh₂</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þunus</span> ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þunwī</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þunus</span> ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þunnī</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þunnuz</span> ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þunnī</span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ln/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ll/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*pl̥h₁nós</span> "full" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*fulnos</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*fullos</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*fullaz</span></span>. This development postdated contact with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samic_languages" title="Samic languages">Samic languages</a>, as is shown by the loanword *pulna &gt; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-Samic" title="Proto-Samic">Proto-Samic</a> *polnē "hill(ock), mound".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aikio06_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aikio06-20">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/zm/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/mm/</span> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*h₁esmi</span> "I am, unstr." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ezmi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*emmi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*immi</span></span></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Unstressed <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/owo/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/oː/</span></b> — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-owos</span> "thematic 1st du." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ōz</span></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Unstressed <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ew/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ow/</span></b> before a consonant or word-finally — <span class="nowrap"><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ews</span> "u-stem gen. sg." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-owz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-auz</span></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span id="Unstressed_.2Fe.2F">/i/"&gt;</span><b>Unstressed <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/e/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/i/</span></b> except before <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/r/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-éteh₂</span> "abstract noun suffix" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-eþā</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-iþā</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-iþō</span>
<ul>
<li>Unstressed <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ej/</span> contracts to <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/iː/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-éys</span> "i-stem gen. sg." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-iys</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-īs</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-īz</span> (with -z by analogy)</li>
