<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/e/</span> before <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/r/</span> later becomes <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɑ/</span> but not until after the application of i-mutation.</li>
<li>Some words that could be unstressed as a whole were also affected, often creating stressed/unstressed pairs — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*éǵh₂</span> "I" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ek</span> &gt; unstressed <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ik</span> (remaining beside stressed <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ek</span>)</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span id="Unstressed_.2Fji.2F">/i/"&gt;</span><b>Unstressed <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ji/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/i/</span></b> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*légʰyeti</span> "(s)he is lying down" ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*légʰyonti</span> "they are lying down" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*legyidi</span> ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*legyondi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*legidi</span> ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*legyondi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ligiþi</span> ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ligjanþi</span> (with -þ- by analogy)
<ul>
<li>The process creates diphthongs from originally disyllabic sequences — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-oyend</span> "thematic optative 3pl" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-oyint</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-oint</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ain</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*áyeri</span> "in the morning" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ayiri</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*airi</span> "early"; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tréyes</span> "three" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þreyiz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þreiz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þrīz</span></li>
<li>The sequence <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/iji/</span> becomes <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/iː/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gʰósteyes</span> "strangers, nom. pl." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gostiyiz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gostīz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gastīz</span> "guests"</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Merging of non-high back vowels</b>:
<ul>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/o/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/a/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɑ/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gʰóstis</span> "stranger" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gostiz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*gastiz</span> "guest"; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kátus</span> "fight" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*haþuz</span> "battle"</li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/oː/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/aː/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɑː/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dʰóh₁mos</span> "thing put" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dōmoz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dāmaz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dōmaz</span> "judgement"; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*swā́dus</span> "sweet" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*swātuz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*swōtuz</span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/oːː/</span>, <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/aːː/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɑːː/</span> (â) — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*séh₁mō</span> "seeds" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sēmô</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sēmâ</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sēmô</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-eh₂es</span> "eh₂-stem nom. pl." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-âz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ôz</span></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_Proto-Germanic">Late Proto-Germanic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Late Proto-Germanic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>By this stage, Germanic had emerged as a distinctive branch and had undergone many of the sound changes that would make its later descendants recognisable as Germanic languages. It had shifted its consonant inventory from a system that was rich in plosives to one containing primarily fricatives, had lost the PIE mobile pitch accent for a predictable stress accent, and had merged two of its vowels. The stress accent had already begun to cause the erosion of unstressed syllables, which would continue in its descendants. The final stage of the language included the remaining development until the breakup into dialects and, most notably, featured the development of nasal vowels and the start of <a href="/wiki/Germanic_umlaut" title="Germanic umlaut">umlaut</a>, another characteristic Germanic feature.</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<td><span id="Word-final_.2Fm.2F_.3E_.2Fn.2F"></span><b>Word-final <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/m/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/n/</span></b> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tóm</span> "that, acc. masc." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þam</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þan</span> "then"; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-om</span> "a-stem acc. sg." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-am</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-an</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ą</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/m/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/n/</span> before dental consonants</b> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ḱm̥tóm</span> "hundred" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*humdan</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hundan</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hundą</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*déḱm̥d</span> "ten" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tehumt</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tehunt</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tehun</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span id="Word-final_.2Fn.2F_is_lost"></span><b>Word-final <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/n/</span> is lost</b> after unstressed syllables, and the preceding vowel is nasalised — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-om</span> "a-stem acc. sg." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-am</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-an</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ą</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-eh₂m</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ān</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ą̄</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ǭ</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-oHom</span> "genitive plural" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ân</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ą̂</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ǫ̂</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Nasal <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ẽː/</span> is lowered</b> to <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɑ̃ː/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dʰédʰeh₁m</span> "I was putting" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dedēn</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dedę̄</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dedą̄</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dedǭ</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Elimination of <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ə/</span></b>:
<ul>
<li>Unstressed <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ə/</span> is lost between consonants — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sámh₂dʰos</span> "sand" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*samədaz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*samdaz</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*takéh₁-</span> "to be silent" &gt; (with added suffix) <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*takəyónti</span> "they are silent" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þagəyanþi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þagyanþi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þagjanþi</span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ə/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɑ/</span> elsewhere — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ph₂tḗr</span> "father" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*fədēr</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*fadēr</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*takéh₁-</span> "to be silent" &gt; (with added suffix) <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*takəyéti</span> "(s)he is silent" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þagəyiþi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þagəiþi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þagaiþi</span></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span id="Loss_of_word-final_.2Ft.2F"></span><b>Loss of word-final <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/t/</span></b> after unstressed syllables — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*déḱm̥d</span> "ten" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tehunt</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tehun</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*bʰéroyd</span> "(s)he would carry, subj." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*berayt</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*berai</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*mélid</span> ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*mélit-</span> "honey" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*melit</span> ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*melid-</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*meli</span> ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*melid-</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*mili</span> ~ <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*milid-</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɣʷ/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/w/</span></b>, sometimes <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɣ/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*snóygʷʰos</span> "snow" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*snaygʷaz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*snaiwaz</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kʷekʷléh₂</span> "wheels (collective)" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hʷegʷlā</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hʷewlā</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hweulō</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Long a is raised</b>:
<ul>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɑː/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɔː/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dʰóh₁mos</span> "thing put" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dāmaz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*dōmaz</span> "judgement"; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*swā́dus</span> "sweet" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*swātuz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*swōtuz</span></li>
<li><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɑːː/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɔːː/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*séh₁mō</span> "seeds" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sēmâ</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sēmô</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-eh₂es</span> "eh₂-stem nom. pl." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-âz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ôz</span></li>
<li>That followed the earliest contact with the Romans since Latin Rōmānī was borrowed as *Rūmānīz and then shifted to *Rūmōnīz.</li>
<li>Finnic loanwords preceding the change are also known:
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a> <i>hake-</i> "to seek", from early Proto-Germanic <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sākija-</span> (later <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sōkija-</span>)</li>
<li>Finnish <i>raha</i> "money", from early Proto-Germanic <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*skrahā</span> "squirrel skin" (later <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*skrahō</span>)</li>
<li>Finnish <i>kavio</i> "hoof", from Pre-Proto-Germanic <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*kāpa-</span> "hoof" (later <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hōfa-</span>)</li>
<li>Finnish <i>lieka</i> "tether", from Pre-Proto-Germanic <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*lēgā-</span> "to lie, be at rest" (later <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*lēgō-</span>, as demonstrated by the later loan <i>lieko</i> "windfallen or decayed tree")</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span id="Early_i-mutation"></span><b>Early <a href="/wiki/I-mutation" title="I-mutation">i-mutation</a></b>: <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/e/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/i/</span> when followed by <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/i/</span> or <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/j/</span> in the same or next syllable — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*bʰéreti</span> "(s)he is carrying" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*beridi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*biridi</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*médʰyos</span> "middle" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*medyaz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*midjaz</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*néwios</span> "new" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*newyaz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*niwjaz</span>
<ul>
<li>This eliminates the remaining <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ei/</span>, changing it to <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/iː/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*deywós</span> "god" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*teywaz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*Tīwaz</span> "<a href="/wiki/T%C3%BDr" title="Týr">Týr</a>"; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*tréyes</span> "three" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þreiz</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þrīz</span></li>
<li>A number of loanwords in the Finnic and Samic demonstrate earlier *e, e.g.
<ul>
<li>Finnish <i>teljo</i> "thwart", from early Proto-Germanic <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þeljō</span> (later <i>*þiljō</i>)</li>
<li>Finnish <i>menninkäinen</i> "goblin", from early Proto-Germanic <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*menþingō</span> (later <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*minþingō</span>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Northern_Sami" title="Northern Sami">Northern Sami</a> <i>deahkki</i> "thick meat", from early Proto-Germanic <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þekkwiz</span> "thick" (later <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*þikkwiz</span>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aikio06_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Aikio06-20">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li>Northern Sami <i>jievja</i> "white (of animal, or hair)", from early Proto-Germanic <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*heują</span> (later <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hiują</span>)</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span id="Pre-nasal_raising"></span><b><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/e/</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/i/</span></b> when followed by a syllable-final nasal — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*en</span> "in" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*in</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*séngʷʰeti</span> "(s)he chants" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sengʷidi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*singwidi</span> "(s)he sings"
<ul>
<li>Finnic loanwords demonstrating earlier *e are again known: Finnish <i>rengas</i> "ring", from early Proto-Germanic <i>*hrengaz</i> (later <i>*hringaz</i>)</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/j/</span> is lost between vowels</b> except after <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/i/</span> and <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/w/</span> (but it is lost after syllabic <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/u/</span>). The two vowels that come to stand in hiatus then contract to long vowels or diphthongs — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-oyh₁m̥</span> "thematic optative 1sg sg." &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-oyum</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-ayų</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*-aų</span>; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*áyeri</span> "in the morning" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ayiri</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*airi</span> "early"
<ul>
<li>This process creates a new <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɑː/</span> from earlier <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/ɑjɑ/</span> — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*steh₂-</span> "to stand" &gt; (with suffix added) <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*sth₂yónti</span> "they stand" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*stayanþi</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*stānþi</span></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span id=".2Fn.2F_is_lost_before_.2Fx.2F"></span><b><span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/n/</span> is lost before <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">/x/</span></b>, causing <a href="/wiki/Compensatory_lengthening" title="Compensatory lengthening">compensatory lengthening</a> and nasalisation of the preceding vowel — <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*ḱónketi</span> "(s)he hangs" &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*hanhidi</span> (phonetically <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">[ˈxɑ̃ːxiði]</span>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lexical_evidence_in_other_language_varieties">Lexical evidence in other language varieties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Lexical evidence in other language varieties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Loans into Proto-Germanic from other (known) languages or from Proto-Germanic into other languages can be dated relative to each other by which Germanic sound laws have acted on them. Since the dates of borrowings and sound laws are not precisely known, it is not possible to use loans to establish absolute or calendar chronology.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Loans_from_adjoining_Indo-European_groups">Loans from adjoining Indo-European groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Loans from adjoining Indo-European groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Most loans from <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic</a> appear to have been made before or during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grimm%27s_Law" title="Grimm's Law">Germanic Sound Shift</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> For instance, one specimen *<i>rīks</i> 'ruler' was borrowed from Celtic *<i>rīxs</i> 'king' (stem *<i>rīg-</i>), with <i>g</i> → <i>k</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> It is clearly not native because PIE *<i>ē</i> → <i>ī</i> is typical of not Germanic but Celtic languages. Another is *<i>walhaz</i> "foreigner; Celt" from the Celtic tribal name <i>Volcae</i> with <i>k</i> → <i>h</i> and <i>o</i> → <i>a</i>. Other likely Celtic loans include *<i>ambahtaz</i> 'servant', *<i>brunjǭ</i> 'mailshirt', *<i>gīslaz</i> 'hostage', *<i>īsarną</i> 'iron', *<i>lēkijaz</i> 'healer', *<i>laudą</i> 'lead', *<i>Rīnaz</i> 'Rhine', and *<i>tūnaz, tūną</i> 'fortified enclosure'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> These loans would likely have been borrowed during the Celtic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hallstatt_Culture" title="Hallstatt Culture">Hallstatt</a> and early <a href="/wiki/La_T%C3%A8ne_culture" title="La Tène culture">La Tène</a> cultures when the Celts dominated central Europe, although the period spanned several centuries.</p>
<p>From <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Iranian" title="East Iranian">East Iranian</a> came *<i>hanapiz</i> 'hemp' (compare <a href="/wiki/Saka_language" title="Saka language">Khotanese</a> <i>kaṃhā</i>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ossetic_language" title="Ossetic language">Ossetian</a> <i>gæn(æ)</i> ‘flax’),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> *<i>humalaz</i>, <i>humalǭ</i> 'hops' (compare Osset <i>xumællæg</i>), *<i>keppǭ</i> ~ <i>skēpą</i> 'sheep' (compare Pers <i>čapiš</i> 'yearling kid'), *<i>kurtilaz</i> 'tunic' (cf. Osset <i>k<sup>w</sup>əræt</i> 'shirt'), *<i>kutą</i> 'cottage' (compare Pers <i>kad</i> 'house'), *<i>paidō</i> 'cloak',<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> *<i>paþaz</i> 'path' (compare <a href="/wiki/Avestan" title="Avestan">Avestan</a> <i>pantā</i>, gen. <i>pathō</i>), and *<i>wurstwa</i> 'work' (compare Av <i>vərəštuua</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> The words could have been transmitted directly by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scythian" title="Scythian">Scythians</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> plain, groups of whom entered Central Europe via the Danube and created the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vekerzug_Culture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vekerzug Culture (page does not exist)">Vekerzug Culture</a> in the Carpathian Basin (6th to 5th centuries BC), or by later contact with Sarmatians, who followed the same route.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> Unsure is *<i>marhaz</i> 'horse', which was either borrowed directly from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scytho-Sarmatian" title="Scytho-Sarmatian">Scytho-Sarmatian</a> or through Celtic mediation.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Loans_into_non-Germanic_languages">Loans into non-Germanic languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Loans into non-Germanic languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(October 2017)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Numerous loanwords believed to have been borrowed from Proto-Germanic are known in the non-Germanic languages spoken in areas adjacent to the Germanic languages.</p>
<p>The heaviest influence has been on the <a href="/wiki/Finnic_languages" title="Finnic languages">Finnic languages</a>, which have received hundreds of Proto-Germanic or pre-Proto-Germanic loanwords.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> Well-known examples include PGmc *<i>druhtinaz</i> 'warlord' (compare Finnish <i>ruhtinas</i>), *<i>hrengaz</i> (later *<i>hringaz</i>) 'ring' (compare Finn <i>rengas</i>, Estonian <i>rõngas</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ringe_2006_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-ringe_2006-30">[29]</a></sup> *<i>kuningaz</i> 'king' (compare Finn <i>kuningas</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Comrie_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Comrie-2">[2]</a></sup> *<i>lambaz</i> 'lamb' (compare Finn <i>lammas</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> *<i>lunaz</i> 'ransom' (compare Finn <i>lunnas</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Loanwords into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samic_languages" title="Samic languages">Samic languages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baltic_languages" title="Baltic languages">Baltic languages</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic languages</a> are also known.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-Indo-European_substrate_elements">Non-Indo-European substrate elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Non-Indo-European substrate elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Germanic_substrate_hypothesis" title="Germanic substrate hypothesis">Germanic substrate hypothesis</a></div>
<p>The term <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Substratum" title="Substratum">substrate</a> with reference to Proto-Germanic refers to lexical items and phonological elements that do not appear to be descended from Proto-Indo-European. The substrate theory postulates that the elements came from an earlier population that stayed amongst the Indo-Europeans and was influential enough to bring over some elements of its own language. The theory of a non-Indo-European substrate was first proposed by <a href="/wiki/Sigmund_Feist" title="Sigmund Feist">Sigmund Feist</a>, who estimated that about a third of all Proto-Germanic lexical items came from the substrate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[note 2]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Theo_Vennemann" title="Theo Vennemann">Theo Vennemann</a> has hypothesized a <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> substrate and a <a href="/wiki/Semitic_languages" title="Semitic languages">Semitic</a> superstrate in Germanic; however, his speculations, too, are generally rejected by specialists in the relevant fields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Research in Germanic etymology continues, and many Germanic words whose origins were previously unclear or controversial now have plausible explanations in terms of reconstructed Indo-European words and morphology. Thus, the proportion of Germanic words without any plausible etymological explanation has decreased over time. Estimates of that proportion are typically outdated or inflated, as many of these proposals were unknown when scholars were compiling lists of unexplained Germanic words.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Phonology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also the <a href="#Phonological_stages_from_Proto-Indo-European_to_end_of_Proto-Germanic">Phonological stages</a> section above.</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transcription">Transcription</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Transcription">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following conventions are used in this article for transcribing Proto-Germanic reconstructed forms:</p>
<ul>
<li>Voiced obstruents appear as <i>b, d, g</i>; this does not imply any particular analysis of the underlying phonemes as plosives <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> or fricatives <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/β/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ð/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɣ/</span>. In other literature, they may be written as <a href="/wiki/Grapheme" title="Grapheme">graphemes</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Bar_(diacritic)" title="Bar (diacritic)">bar</a> to produce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B_with_stroke" title="B with stroke">ƀ</a>, <a href="/wiki/D_with_stroke" title="D with stroke">đ</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C7%A4" title="Ǥ">ǥ</a>.</li>
<li>Unvoiced fricatives appear as <i>f, þ, h</i> (perhaps <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɸ/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/θ/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x/</span>). <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x/</span> may have become <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/h/</span> in certain positions at a later stage of Proto-Germanic itself. Similarly for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/xʷ/</span>, which later became <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/hʷ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʍ/</span> in some environments.</li>
<li>Labiovelars appear as <i>kw, hw, gw</i>; this does not imply any particular analysis as single sounds (e.g. <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʷ/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/xʷ/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡʷ/</span>) or clusters (e.g. <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kw/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/xw/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡw/</span>).</li>
<li>The yod sound appears as <i>j</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span>. Note that the normal convention for representing this sound in <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a> is <i>y</i>; the use of <i>j</i> does not imply any actual change in the pronunciation of the sound.</li>
<li>Long vowels are denoted with a macron over the letter, e.g. <i>ō</i>. When a distinction is necessary, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛː/</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eː/</span> are transcribed as <i>ē¹</i> and <i>ē²</i> respectively. <i>ē¹</i> is sometimes transcribed as <i>æ</i> or <i>ǣ</i> instead, but this is not followed here.</li>
<li>Overlong vowels appear with circumflexes, e.g. <i>ô</i>. In other literature they are often denoted by a doubled macron, e.g. <i>ō̄</i>.</li>
<li>Nasal vowels are written here with an <a href="/wiki/Ogonek" title="Ogonek">ogonek</a>, following Don Ringe's usage, e.g. <i>ǫ̂</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/õːː/</span>. Most commonly in literature, they are denoted simply by a following n. However, this can cause confusion between a word-final nasal vowel and a word-final regular vowel followed by <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span>, a distinction which was phonemic. Tildes (ã, ĩ, ũ...) are also used in some sources.</li>
<li>Diphthongs appear as <i>ai, au, eu, iu, ōi, ōu</i> and perhaps <i>ēi, ēu</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> However, when immediately followed by the corresponding semivowel, they appear as <i>ajj, aww, eww, iww</i>. <i>u</i> is written as <i>w</i> when between a vowel and <i>j</i>. This convention is based on the usage in <a href="#CITEREFRinge2006">Ringe 2006</a>.</li>
<li>Long vowels followed by a non-high vowel were separate syllables and are written as such here, except for <i>ī</i>, which is written <i>ij</i> in that case.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consonants">Consonants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Consonants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The table below<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">[4]</a></sup> lists the consonantal phonemes of Proto-Germanic classified by their reconstructed pronunciation. The slashes around the phonemes are omitted for clarity. When two phonemes appear in the same box, the first of each pair is voiceless, the second is voiced. Phones written in parentheses represent <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">allophones</a> and are not independent phonemes. For descriptions of the sounds and definitions of the terms, follow the links on the headings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[note 3]</a></sup></p>

<p>Notes:</p>
<ol>
<li><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ŋ]</span> was an allophone of <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span> before velar obstruents.</li>
<li><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ŋʷ]</span> was an allophone of <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span> before labiovelar obstruents.</li>
<li><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[β]</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ð]</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɣ]</span> were allophones of <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> in certain positions (see below).</li>
<li>The phoneme written as <i>f</i> was probably still realised as a bilabial fricative (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɸ/</span>) in Proto-Germanic. Evidence for this is the fact that in Gothic, word-final b (which medially represents a voiced fricative) devoices to <i>f</i> and also Old Norse spellings such as <i>aptr</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɑɸtr]</span>, where the letter <i>p</i> rather than the more usual <i>f</i> was used to denote the bilabial realisation before <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t/</span>.</li>
</ol>
<h4><span id="Grimm's_and_Verner's_law"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Grimm.27s_and_Verner.27s_law">Grimm's and Verner's law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Grimm's and Verner's law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Grimm%27s_law" title="Grimm's law">Grimm's law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Verner%27s_law" title="Verner's law">Verner's law</a></div>
<p>Grimm's law as applied to pre-proto-Germanic is a <a href="/wiki/Chain_shift" title="Chain shift">chain shift</a> of the original Indo-European <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plosives" title="Plosives">plosives</a>. Verner's Law explains a category of exceptions to Grimm's Law, where a voiced fricative appears where Grimm's Law predicts a voiceless fricative. The discrepancy is conditioned by the placement of the original Indo-European word accent.</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th></th>
<th><b>Labiovelar reduction (near u)</b></th>
<th><b>Grimm's law: Voiceless to fricative</b></th>
<th><b>Grimm's law: Voiced to voiceless</b></th>
<th><b>Grimm's law: Aspirated to voiced</b></th>
<th><b>Verner's law</b></th>
<th><b>Labiovelar dissolution</b></th>
</tr>

<td><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">b</span> &gt; <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">p</span></td>

<td><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɡʱ</span> &gt; <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɡ</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɣ</span></td>

<td></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>labiovelars</b></td>
<td><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">kʷ</span> &gt; <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">k</span><br/>
<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɡʷ</span> &gt; <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɡ</span><br/>
<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɡʷʱ</span> &gt; <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɡʱ</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">kʷ</span> &gt; <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">xʷ</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɡʷ</span> &gt; <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">kʷ</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɡʷʱ</span> &gt; <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɡʷ</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɣʷ</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">xʷ</span> &gt; <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɡʷ</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɣʷ</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɡʷ</span> &gt; <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">b</span><br/>
<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɣʷ</span> &gt; <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">w</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɣ</span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>p</i>, <i>t</i>, and <i>k</i> did not undergo Grimm's law after a fricative (such as <i>s</i>) or after other plosives (which were shifted to fricatives by the Germanic spirant law); for example, where Latin (with the original <i>t</i>) has <i>stella</i> "star" and <i>octō</i> "eight", Middle Dutch has <i>ster</i> and <i>acht</i> (with unshifted <i>t</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup> This original <i>t</i> merged with the shifted <i>t</i> from the voiced consonant; that is, most of the instances of /t/ came from either the original /t/ or the shifted /t/.</p>
<p>(A similar shift on the consonant inventory of Proto-Germanic later generated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_German" title="High German">High German</a>. McMahon says:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>"Grimm's and Verner's Laws ... together form the First Germanic Consonant Shift. A second, and chronologically later Second Germanic Consonant Shift ... affected only Proto-Germanic voiceless stops ... and split Germanic into two sets of dialects, <a href="/wiki/Low_German" title="Low German">Low German</a> in the north ... and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_German" title="High German">High German</a> further south ...")</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Verner's law is usually reconstructed as following Grimm's law in time, and states that unvoiced fricatives: <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɸ/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/θ/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x/</span> are voiced when preceded by an unaccented syllable. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accent_(phonology)" title="Accent (phonology)">accent</a> at the time of the change was the one inherited from Proto-Indo-European, which was free and could occur on any syllable. For example, PIE <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*bʰréh₂tēr</span> &gt; PGmc. *brōþēr "brother" but PIE <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*meh₂tḗr</span> &gt; PGmc. *mōdēr "mother". The voicing of some <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> according to Verner's Law produced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/z/</span>, a new phoneme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">[4]</a></sup> Sometime after Grimm's and Verner's law, Proto-Germanic lost its inherited contrastive accent, and all words became stressed on their root syllable. This was generally the first syllable unless a prefix was attached.</p>
<p>The loss of the Proto-Indo-European contrastive accent got rid of the conditioning environment for the consonant alternations created by Verner's law. Without this conditioning environment, the cause of the alternation was no longer obvious to native speakers. The alternations that had started as mere phonetic variants of sounds became increasingly grammatical in nature, leading to the grammatical alternations of sounds known as <a href="/wiki/Grammatischer_Wechsel" title="Grammatischer Wechsel">Grammatischer Wechsel</a>. For a single word, the grammatical stem could display different consonants depending on its grammatical case or its tense. As a result of the complexity of this system, significant levelling of these sounds occurred throughout the Germanic period as well as in the later daughter languages. Already in Proto-Germanic, most alternations in nouns were leveled to have only one sound or the other consistently throughout all forms of a word, although some alternations were preserved, only to be levelled later in the daughters (but differently in each one). Alternations in noun and verb endings were also levelled, usually in favour of the voiced alternants in nouns, but a split remained in verbs where unsuffixed (strong) verbs received the voiced alternants while suffixed (weak) verbs had the voiceless alternants. Alternation between the present and past of strong verbs remained common and was not levelled in Proto-Germanic, and survives up to the present day in some Germanic languages.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Allophones">Allophones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Allophones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Some of the consonants that developed from the sound shifts are thought to have been pronounced in different ways (allophones) depending on the sounds around them. With regard to original <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʷ/</span> Trask says:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>"The resulting <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/xʷ/</span> were reduced to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/h/</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/hʷ/</span> in word-initial position."</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Many of the consonants listed in the table could appear lengthened or prolonged under some circumstances, which is inferred from their appearing in some daughter languages as doubled <a href="/wiki/Grapheme" title="Grapheme">letters</a>. This phenomenon is termed <a href="/wiki/Gemination" title="Gemination">gemination</a>. Kraehenmann says:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[37]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>"Then, Proto-Germanic already had long consonants … but they contrasted with short ones only word-medially. Moreover, they were not very frequent and occurred only intervocally almost exclusively after short vowels."</p>
</blockquote>
<p>The voiced phonemes <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡʷ/</span> are reconstructed with the pronunciation of stops in some environments and fricatives in others. The pattern of allophony is not completely clear, but generally is similar to the patterns of voiced obstruent allophones in languages such as Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup> The voiced fricatives of Verner's Law (see above), which only occurred in non-word-initial positions, merged with the fricative allophones of <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡʷ/</span>. Older accounts tended to suggest that the sounds were originally fricatives and later "hardened" into stops in some circumstances. However, Ringe notes that this belief was largely due to theory-internal considerations of older phonological theories, and in modern theories it is equally possible that the allophony was present from the beginning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Each of the three voiced phonemes <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span>, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> had a slightly different pattern of allophony from the others, but in general stops occurred in "strong" positions (word-initial and in clusters) while fricatives occurred in "weak" positions (post-vocalic). More specifically:</p>
<ul>
<li>Word-initial <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span> were stops <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[b]</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[d]</span>.</li>
<li>A good deal of evidence, however, indicates that word-initial <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> was <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɣ]</span>, subsequently developing to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɡ]</span> in a number of languages. This is clearest from developments in <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Frisian_languages" title="Anglo-Frisian languages">Anglo-Frisian</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Ingvaeonic_languages" title="Ingvaeonic languages">Ingvaeonic languages</a>. Modern Dutch still preserves the sound of <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɣ]</span> in this position.</li>
<li>Plosives appeared after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homorganic" title="Homorganic">homorganic</a> nasal consonants: <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[mb]</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[nd]</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ŋɡ]</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ŋʷɡʷ]</span>. This was the only place where a voiced labiovelar <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɡʷ]</span> could still occur.</li>
<li>When geminate, they were pronounced as stops <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[bb]</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[dd]</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɡɡ]</span>. This rule continued to apply at least into the early West Germanic languages, since the <a href="/wiki/West_Germanic_gemination" title="West Germanic gemination">West Germanic gemination</a> produced geminated plosives from earlier voiced fricatives.</li>
<li><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span> was <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[d]</span> after /l/ or /z/. Evidence for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span> after <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/r/</span> is conflicting: it appears as a plosive in Gothic <i>waurd</i> "word" (not *<i>waurþ</i>, with devoicing), but as a fricative in Old Norse <i>orð</i>. <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span> hardened to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[d]</span> in all positions in the <a href="/wiki/West_Germanic_languages" title="West Germanic languages">West Germanic languages</a>.</li>
<li>In other positions, fricatives occurred singly after vowels and diphthongs, and after non-nasal consonants in the case of <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/g/</span>.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Labiovelars">Labiovelars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Labiovelars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Numerous additional changes affected the labiovelar consonants.</p>
<ol>
<li>Even before the operation of <a href="/wiki/Grimm%27s_law" title="Grimm's law">Grimm's law</a>, they were reduced to plain velars next to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span> due to the <a href="/wiki/Bouk%C3%B3los_rule" title="Boukólos rule">boukólos rule</a> of PIE. This rule continued to operate as a <a href="/wiki/Surface_filter" title="Surface filter">surface filter</a>, i.e. if a sound change generated a new environment in which a labiovelar occurred near a <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span>, it was immediately converted to a plain velar. This caused certain alternations in verb paradigms, such as *<i>singwaną</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[siŋʷɡʷɑnɑ̃]</span> ('to sing') versus *<i>sungun</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[suŋɡun]</span> ('they sang'). Apparently, this delabialization also occurred with labiovelars following <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/un/</span>, showing that the language possessed a labial allophone <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ŋʷ]</span> as well. In this case the entire clusters <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[uŋʷxʷ]</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[uŋʷkʷ]</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[uŋʷgʷ]</span> are delabialized to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[uŋx]</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[uŋk]</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[uŋg]</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>After the operation of <a href="/wiki/Verner%27s_law" title="Verner's law">Verner's law</a>, various changes conspired to almost completely eliminate voiced labiovelars. Initially, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɡʷʰ]</span> became <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[b]</span>, e.g. PIE *<span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">gʷʱédʱyeti</span> &gt; PGmc. bidiþi "(s)he asks for". The fricative variant <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɣʷ]</span> (which occurred in most non-initial environments) usually became <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[w]</span>, but sometimes instead turned into <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɣ]</span>. The only environment in which a voiced labiovelar remained was after a nasal, e.g. in *<i>singwaną</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[siŋʷɡʷɑnɑ̃]</span> "to sing". These various changes often led to complex alternations, e.g. *<i>sehwaną</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[sexʷɑnɑ̃]</span> ('to see'), *<i>sēgun</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[sɛːɣun]</span> ('they saw', indicative), *<i>sēwīn</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[sɛːwiːn]</span> ('they saw', subjunctive), which were reanalysed and regularised differently in the various daughter languages.</li>
</ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Consonant_gradation">Consonant gradation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Consonant gradation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Kroonen (2011) posits a process of <a href="/wiki/Consonant_mutation" title="Consonant mutation">consonant mutation</a> for Proto-Germanic, under the name <i>consonant gradation</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup> (This is distinct from the consonant mutation processes occurring in the neighboring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samic_languages" title="Samic languages">Samic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Finnic_languages" title="Finnic languages">Finnic</a> languages, also known as <a href="/wiki/Consonant_gradation" title="Consonant gradation">consonant gradation</a> since the 19th century.) The Proto-Germanic consonant gradation is not directly attested in any of the Germanic dialects, but may nevertheless be reconstructed on the basis of certain dialectal discrepancies in root of the <i>n</i>-stems and the <i>ōn</i>-verbs.</p>
<p>Diachronically, the rise of consonant gradation in Germanic can be explained by <a href="/wiki/Kluge%27s_law" title="Kluge's law">Kluge's law</a>, by which geminates arose from stops followed by a nasal in a stressed syllable. Since this sound law only operated in part of the paradigms of the <i>n</i>-stems and <i>ōn</i>-verbs, it gave rise to an alternation of geminated and non-geminated consonants. However, there has been controversy about the validity of this law, with some linguists preferring to explain the development of geminate consonants with the idea of "expressive gemination". The origin of the Germanic geminate consonants is currently a disputed part of historical linguistics with no clear consensus at present.</p>
<table class="wikitable IPA">
<tr>
<th><i>n</i>-stems</th>
<th>PIE</th>
<th>PGM</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>nominative</td>
<td>C_́C-ōn</td>
<td>C_C-ō</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>genitive</td>
<td>C_C-n-ós</td>
<td>C_CC-az</td>
</tr>
</table>
<table class="wikitable IPA">
<tr>
<th><i>neh<sub>2</sub></i>-presents</th>
<th>PIE</th>
<th>PGM</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>3p. singular</td>
<td>C_C-néh<sub>2</sub>-ti</td>
<td>C_CC-ōþi</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>3p. plural</td>
<td>C_C-nh<sub>2</sub>-énti</td>
<td>C_G-unanþi</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The reconstruction of <i>grading</i> paradigms in Proto-Germanic explains root alternations such as Old English <i>steorra</i> 'star' &lt; *<i>sterran-</i> vs. Old Frisian <i>stera</i> 'id.' &lt; *<i>steran-</i> and Norwegian (dial.) <i>guva</i> 'to swing' &lt; *<i>gubōn-</i> vs. Middle High German <i>gupfen</i> 'id.' &lt; *<i>guppōn-</i> as generalizations of the original allomorphy. In the cases concerned, this would imply reconstructing an <i>n</i>-stem nom. *<i>sterō</i>, gen. *<i>sterraz</i> &lt; PIE *<i>h<sub>2</sub>stér-ōn</i>, *<i>h<sub>2</sub>ster-n-ós</i> and an <i>ōn</i>-verb 3sg. *<i>guppōþi</i>, 3pl. *<i>gubunanþi</i> &lt; *<i>g<sup>h</sup>ub<sup>h</sup>-néh<sub>2</sub>-ti</i>, *<i>g<sup>h</sup>ub<sup>h</sup>-nh<sub>2</sub>-énti</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">Vowels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Proto-Germanic_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Vowels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Proto-Germanic had four short vowels,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup> five or six long vowels, and at least one "overlong" or "trimoric" vowel. The exact phonetic quality of the vowels is uncertain.</p>
